895 <section id="_1">

896

897 <h2>

898General Information About Chronic Lymphocytic Leukemia (CLL)</h2>

899

900 <div id="_section_1" class="pdq-sections">

901<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

902<h6>

903In This Section</h6>

904<ul>

905<li>

906<a href="#_235_toc">

907Incidence and Mortality</a>

908</li>

909<li>

910<a href="#_710_toc">

911Anatomy</a>

912</li>

913<li>

914<a href="#_583_toc">

915Clinical Presentation</a>

916</li>

917<li>

918<a href="#_585_toc">

919Diagnostic Evaluation and Differential Diagnosis</a>

920</li>

921<li>

922<a href="#_593_toc">

923Prognostic Factors</a>

924</li>

925<li>

926<a href="#_600_toc">

927Follow-Up After Treatment</a>

928</li>

929</ul>

930</nav>

931<div class="pdq-hp-patient-toggle">

932<a href="/types/leukemia/patient/cll-treatment-pdq">

933Go to Patient Version</a>

934</div>

935<section id="_235">

936<h3 id="_235_toc">

937Incidence and Mortality</h3>

938<p id="_236" tabindex="-1">

939Estimated new cases and deaths from CLL in the United States in 2023:[<a href="#cit/section_1.1">

9401</a>

941]</p>

942<div class="pdq-content-list">

943<ul id="_237">

944<li>

945New cases: 18,740.</li>

946<li>

947Deaths: 4,490.</li>

948</ul>

949</div>

950</section>

951<section id="_710">

952<h3 id="_710_toc">

953Anatomy</h3>

954<p id="_711" tabindex="-1">

955CLL is a disorder of morphologically mature, but

956immunologically less mature lymphocytes. It is manifested by progressive

957accumulation of these cells in the blood, bone marrow, and lymphatic tissues.[<a href="#cit/section_1.2">

9582</a>

959]</p>

960<figure id="figure_580" class="image-center">

961<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/526538.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

962Enlarge</a>

963<img id="_580" alt="Blood cell development; drawing shows the steps a blood stem cell goes through to become a red blood cell, platelet, or white blood cell. A myeloid stem cell becomes a red blood cell, a platelet, or a myeloblast, which then becomes a granulocyte (the types of granulocytes are eosinophils, basophils, and neutrophils). A lymphoid stem cell becomes a lymphoblast and then becomes a B-lymphocyte, T-lymphocyte, or natural killer cell." title="Blood cell development; drawing shows the steps a blood stem cell goes through to become a red blood cell, platelet, or white blood cell. A myeloid stem cell becomes a red blood cell, a platelet, or a myeloblast, which then becomes a granulocyte (the types of granulocytes are eosinophils, basophils, and neutrophils). A lymphoid stem cell becomes a lymphoblast and then becomes a B-lymphocyte, T-lymphocyte, or natural killer cell." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/526538-750.jpg">

964<figcaption class="caption-container">

965Blood cell development. A blood stem cell goes through several steps to become a red blood cell, platelet, or white blood cell. </figcaption>

966</figure>

967</section>

968<section id="_583">

969<h3 id="_583_toc">

970Clinical Presentation</h3>

971<p id="_584" tabindex="-1">

972The clinical course of this

973disease progresses from an indolent lymphocytosis without other evident disease

974to one of generalized lymphatic enlargement with concomitant pancytopenia.

975Complications of pancytopenia, including hemorrhage and infection, represent a

976major cause of death in these patients.[<a href="#cit/section_1.3">

9773</a>

978] Immunological aberrations,

979including Coombs-positive hemolytic anemia, immune thrombocytopenia, and

980depressed immunoglobulin levels may all complicate the management of CLL.[<a href="#cit/section_1.4">

9814</a>

982]</p>

983</section>

984<section id="_585">

985<h3 id="_585_toc">

986Diagnostic Evaluation and Differential Diagnosis</h3>

987<p id="_586" tabindex="-1">

988Tests and procedures used to diagnose CLL include the following:[<a href="#cit/section_1.5">

9895</a>

990]</p>

991<div class="pdq-content-list">

992<ul id="_587">

993<li>

994History and physical examination (including bidimensional diameters of the largest palpable lymph nodes in the cervical, axillary, and inguinal nodal sites and dimensions of the liver and spleen below their respective costal margins as assessed by palpation).</li>

995<li>

996Complete blood count with differential and chemistry panel (including creatinine, bilirubin, transaminases, and alkaline phosphatase). Other blood tests may include lactate dehydrogenase and beta-2-microglobulin. With suspicion of autoimmune hemolytic anemia, testing for reticulocyte count, indirect bilirubin, serum haptoglobin, antiglobulin (direct Coombs), and cold agglutinin may be helpful.</li>

997<li>

998Flow cytometry (for immunophenotyping).</li>

999<li>

1000Fluorescence <em>

1001in situ</em>

1002 hybridization (FISH) (for del(11q), del(13q), del(17p), trisomy 12, and t(11;14)).</li>

1003<li>

1004<em class="gene-name">

1005TP53</em>

1006 mutation analysis.</li>

1007<li>

1008<em class="gene-name">

1009IgVH</em>

1010 mutation analysis.</li>

1011<li>

1012Serum immunoglobulin levels.</li>

1013<li>

1014Hepatitis B and C and HIV tests.</li>

1015<li>

1016Computed tomography (CT) is usually not required in the absence of peripheral adenopathy; extensive adenopathy on examination should prompt investigation of retroperitoneal adenopathy.</li>

1017<li>

1018Bone marrow aspiration and biopsy is usually not required.</li>

1019</ul>

1020</div>

1021<p id="_588" tabindex="-1">

1022In this disorder, lymphocyte counts in the blood are usually greater than or equal to 5,000/mm<span class="sup">

10233</span>

1024 with a characteristic immunophenotype (CD5- and CD23-positive B cells).[<a href="#cit/section_1.6">

10256</a>

1026,<a href="#cit/section_1.7">

10277</a>

1028]

1029 As assays have become more sensitive for detecting monoclonal B-CLL&#8211;like cells in peripheral blood, researchers have detected a monoclonal B-cell lymphocytosis in 3% of adults older than 40 years and in 6% of adults older than 60 years.[<a href="#cit/section_1.8">

10308</a>

1031] Such early detection and diagnosis may falsely suggest improved survival for the group and may unnecessarily worry or result in therapy for some patients who would have remained undiagnosed in their lifetime, a circumstance known as overdiagnosis or pseudodisease.[<a href="#cit/section_1.9">

10329</a>

1033,<a href="#cit/section_1.10">

103410</a>

1035]</p>

1036<p id="_589" tabindex="-1">

1037Confusion with other diseases may be avoided by determination of cell surface

1038markers. CLL lymphocytes coexpress the B-cell antigens CD19 and CD20 along

1039with the T-cell antigen CD5.[<a href="#cit/section_1.11">

104011</a>

1041] This coexpression occurs in only one other

1042disease entity, mantle cell lymphoma. CLL B cells express relatively low

1043levels of surface-membrane immunoglobulin (compared with normal peripheral

1044blood B cells) and a single light chain (kappa or lambda).[<a href="#cit/section_1.12">

104512</a>

1046] CLL is diagnosed

1047by an absolute increase in lymphocytosis and/or bone marrow infiltration

1048coupled with the characteristic features of morphology and immunophenotype, which confirm the characteristic clonal population. In a database analysis, for up to 77 months before diagnosis, almost all patients with a CLL diagnosis had prediagnostic B-cell clones that were identified in peripheral blood (when available).[<a href="#cit/section_1.7">

10497</a>

1050,<a href="#cit/section_1.13">

105113</a>

1052]</p>

1053<p id="_605" tabindex="-1">

1054About 1% of morphological CLL cases express T-cell markers (CD4 and CD7) and have

1055clonal rearrangements of their T-cell receptor genes. These patients have a

1056higher frequency of skin lesions, more variable lymphocyte shape, and shorter

1057median survival (13 months) with minimal responses to chemotherapy and B-cell receptor inhibitors.[<a href="#cit/section_1.14">

105814</a>

1059]</p>

1060<p id="_590" tabindex="-1">

1061The differential diagnosis must exclude the following:</p>

1062<div class="pdq-content-list">

1063<ul id="_591">

1064<li>

1065<strong>

1066Monoclonal B-cell lymphocytosis (MBL).</strong>

1067 MBL, the precursor to CLL, is defined as a clonal B-cell population circulating in peripheral blood with fewer than 5 &#215; 10<span class="sup">

10689</span>

1069/L B cells and no signs of lymphadenopathy or splenomegaly.[<a href="#cit/section_1.15">

107015</a>

1071] Most cases have the immunophenotype of CLL. The incidence of MBL in the general population is 5% to 12% and increases with age.[<a href="#cit/section_1.16">

107216</a>

1073] In families with two or more cases of CLL, MBL has a prevalence of 13% to 18%. Low-count MBL (&#8804;0.5 &#215; 10<span class="sup">

10749</span>

1075/L B cells) rarely progresses to overt CLL, but higher levels can progress to symptomatic CLL at a rate of less than 2% per year, even for familial cases.[<a href="#cit/section_1.15">

107615</a>

1077,<a href="#cit/section_1.17">

107817</a>

1079] In two selected series of more than 900 patients monitored prospectively for a median of 5 to 7 years, overt CLL requiring chemotherapy occurred in 7% of patients.[<a href="#cit/section_1.8">

10808</a>

1081,<a href="#cit/section_1.18">

108218</a>

1083] A screening study using the Mayo Clinic Biobank identified 1,712 patients with MBL from 10,139 screened samples.[<a href="#cit/section_1.19">

108419</a>

1085] Low-count MBL was found in 95% of these patients. With a median follow-up of 10.0 years, only 0.58% of patients progressed to a lymphoid malignancy.[<a href="#cit/section_1.19">

108619</a>

1087]</li>

1088<li>

1089<strong>

1090Hairy cell leukemia.</strong>

1091 For more information, see <a href="/types/leukemia/hp/hairy-cell-treatment-pdq">

1092Hairy Cell Leukemia Treatment</a>

1093.</li>

1094<li>

1095<strong>

1096Waldenstr&#246;m macroglobulinemia.</strong>

1097 Waldenstr&#246;m

1098macroglobulinemia has a natural history and therapeutic options similar to CLL,

1099with the exception of hyperviscosity syndrome associated with macroglobulinemia

1100as a result of elevated immunoglobulin M. For more information, see <a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/b-cell-lymphoma-treatment-pdq">

1101B-Cell Non-Hodgkin Lymphoma Treatment</a>

1102.</li>

1103<li>

1104<strong>

1105Prolymphocytic leukemia (PLL).</strong>

1106 PLL is a

1107rare form of lymphocytic leukemia characterized by excessive prolymphocytes in the blood with a

1108typical phenotype that is positive for CD19, CD20, and surface-membrane

1109immunoglobulin and negative for CD5.[<a href="#cit/section_1.20">

111020</a>

1111] These patients demonstrate splenomegaly

1112and poor response to low-dose or high-dose chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_1.12">

111312</a>

1114,<a href="#cit/section_1.21">

111521</a>

1116]<p id="_592" tabindex="-1">

1117Cladribine

1118(2-chlorodeoxyadenosine) appears to be an active agent (60% complete remission

1119rate) for patients with de novo B-cell PLL.[<a href="#cit/section_1.22">

112022</a>

1121][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

1122Level of evidence C3</a>

1123] Anecdotal responses have been seen with venetoclax.[<a href="#cit/section_1.23">

112423</a>

1125][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

1126Level of evidence C3</a>

1127] Alemtuzumab, an anti-CD52 humanized monoclonal antibody, has been used for 76 patients with T-cell PLL after failure of previous chemotherapy (usually pentostatin or cladribine). The response rate was 51% (95% confidence interval, 40%&#8211;63%) and the median time to progression was 4.5 months (range, 0.1&#8211;45.4 months).[<a href="#cit/section_1.24">

112824</a>

1129][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

1130Level of evidence C3</a>

1131] These response rates have been confirmed by other investigators.[<a href="#cit/section_1.25">

113225</a>

1133] Patients with CLL who show prolymphocytoid transformation

1134maintain the classic CLL phenotype and have a worse prognosis than PLL

1135patients.</p>

1136</li>

1137<li>

1138<strong>

1139Large granular lymphocyte (LGL) leukemia.</strong>

1140 LGL leukemia is characterized by

1141lymphocytosis with a natural killer (NK) cell immunophenotype (CD2, CD16, and CD56)

1142or a T-cell immunophenotype (CD2, CD3, and CD8).[<a href="#cit/section_1.26">

114326</a>

1144-<a href="#cit/section_1.28">

114528</a>

1146] These patients often

1147have neutropenia and a history of rheumatoid arthritis. The natural history is

1148indolent, often marked by anemia and splenomegaly. This condition appears to

1149fit into the clinical spectrum of Felty syndrome.[<a href="#cit/section_1.29">

115029</a>

1151] A characteristic genetic finding in almost 50% of the patients with T-cell LGL involves mutations in the <em class="gene-name">

1152STAT3</em>

1153 gene.[<a href="#cit/section_1.30">

115430</a>

1155] Symptomatic patients with cytopenias typically manifest CD8-positive T cells with alpha/beta surface receptors plus a <em class="gene-name">

1156STAT3</em>

1157 mutation, CD8-positive T cells with T gamma/delta surface receptors, or a mutated NK T-cell phenotype.[<a href="#cit/section_1.31">

115831</a>

1159] Conversely, asymptomatic patients have wild-type <em class="gene-name">

1160STAT3</em>

1161 CD8-positive T cells, CD4-positive T cells, and wild-type NK cells.[<a href="#cit/section_1.31">

116231</a>

1163] Therapy includes

1164low doses of oral cyclophosphamide or methotrexate, cyclosporine, and treatment of

1165the bacterial infections acquired during severe neutropenia.[<a href="#cit/section_1.26">

116626</a>

1167,<a href="#cit/section_1.28">

116828</a>

1169,<a href="#cit/section_1.32">

117032</a>

1171,<a href="#cit/section_1.33">

117233</a>

1173]</li>

1174</ul>

1175</div>

1176</section>

1177<section id="_593">

1178<h3 id="_593_toc">

1179Prognostic Factors</h3>

1180<p id="_181" tabindex="-1">

1181Prognostic markers help stratify patients in clinical trials, assess the need for therapy, and select the type of therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_1.2">

11822</a>

1183,<a href="#cit/section_1.34">

118434</a>

1185,<a href="#cit/section_1.35">

118635</a>

1187] Prognostic factors that may help predict clinical outcome include cytogenetic

1188subgroup, immunoglobulin mutational status, and CD38 immunophenotype.[<a href="#cit/section_1.2">

11892</a>

1190,<a href="#cit/section_1.36">

119136</a>

1192-<a href="#cit/section_1.44">

119344</a>

1194]</p>

1195<p id="_594" tabindex="-1">

1196Prognostic markers include the following:</p>

1197<div class="pdq-content-list">

1198<ul id="_182">

1199<li>

1200<strong>

1201<em class="gene-name">

1202IgVH</em>

1203 mutation.</strong>

1204[<a href="#cit/section_1.37">

120537</a>

1206-<a href="#cit/section_1.39">

120739</a>

1208,<a href="#cit/section_1.44">

120944</a>

1210,<a href="#cit/section_1.45">

121145</a>

1212] The finding of significant numbers of mutations in this region is associated with a median survival in excess of 20 to 25 years. The absence of mutations is associated with a median survival of 8 to 10 years.</li>

1213<li>

1214<strong>

1215FISH test results.</strong>

1216 FISH chromosomal abnormalities were associated with prognosis in retrospective and prospective studies and clonal evolution has been seen over time.[<a href="#cit/section_1.36">

121736</a>

1218,<a href="#cit/section_1.46">

121946</a>

1220-<a href="#cit/section_1.48">

122148</a>

1222] The following chromosomal abnormalities have been reported:<div class="pdq-content-list">

1223<ul id="_712">

1224<li>

1225 del(13q) is a favorable prognostic marker (median overall survival [OS], 17 years in one prospective study).[<a href="#cit/section_1.48">

122648</a>

1227]</li>

1228<li>

1229Trisomy 12 and del(11) have a less favorable prognosis (median OS, 9&#8211;11 years in one prospective study).[<a href="#cit/section_1.48">

123048</a>

1231]</li>

1232<li>

1233del(17p) is associated with mutated <em class="gene-name">

1234TP53</em>

1235 and with poor response rates and short duration of response to the standard therapeutic options.[<a href="#cit/section_1.44">

123644</a>

1237] del(17p) is associated with the most unfavorable prognosis (median OS, 7 years in one prospective trial).[<a href="#cit/section_1.48">

123848</a>

1239-<a href="#cit/section_1.50">

124050</a>

1241]</li>

1242<li>

1243The combination of adverse cytogenetics, such as del(11q) or del(17p) deletion (suggesting a worse prognosis), with zeta-chain-associated protein 70 kDa negativity (suggesting a better prognosis) in the same patients resulted in a poor prognosis.[<a href="#cit/section_1.43">

124443</a>

1245]</li>

1246</ul>

1247</div>

1248<p id="_713" tabindex="-1">

1249These findings emphasize the need for prospective studies of combinations of these prognostic markers.[<a href="#cit/section_1.51">

125051</a>

1251]</p>

1252 </li>

1253</ul>

1254</div>

1255<p id="_597" tabindex="-1">

1256Other prognostic factors include the following:</p>

1257<div class="pdq-content-list">

1258<ul id="_598">

1259<li>

1260<strong>

1261Anemia and thrombocytopenia.</strong>

1262 These are important adverse prognostic variables, but only if due to extensive marrow involvement by CLL. Autoimmune hemolytic anemia and immune thrombocytopenic purpura do not confer a worse prognosis.</li>

1263<li>

1264<strong>

1265Age.</strong>

1266 CLL occurs primarily in middle-aged and older adults, with worse prognosis in successive decades of life.[<a href="#cit/section_1.47">

126747</a>

1268]</li>

1269<li>

1270<strong>

1271Stage.</strong>

1272[<a href="#cit/section_1.52">

127352</a>

1274,<a href="#cit/section_1.53">

127553</a>

1276] For more information, see the sections on the <a href="/types/leukemia/hp/cll-treatment-pdq#_10">

1277Rai Staging System</a>

1278 and the <a href="/types/leukemia/hp/cll-treatment-pdq#_21">

1279Binet Classification</a>

1280.</li>

1281<li>

1282<strong>

1283Positron emission tomography (PET)-CT scan results.</strong>

1284 This test should only be used in the context of recurrent fever, soaking night sweats, weight loss (&gt;10% baseline weight in 6 months), or rapidly growing lymph nodes, because these findings might herald histological transformation to a diffuse large B-cell lymphoma (so-called Richter transformation). Of 432 patients retrospectively reviewed, 209 patients had a maximum standardized uptake value (SUV<sub>

1285max</sub>

1286) of 5 or higher.[<a href="#cit/section_1.54">

128754</a>

1288] Eighty percent of these patients had histologically aggressive CLL or Richter syndrome, and both of these entities had equally worse prognoses. When the SUV<sub>

1289max</sub>

1290 was 10 or higher, the 5-year OS rate was only 30%.[<a href="#cit/section_1.54">

129154</a>

1292]</li>

1293<li>

1294<strong>

1295Lymphocyte doubling time.</strong>

1296 Doubling of the white blood cell count in less than 1 year implies a worse prognosis.[<a href="#cit/section_1.55">

129755</a>

1298]</li>

1299<li>

1300<strong>

1301Beta-2-microglobulin.</strong>

1302 Higher levels imply a worse prognosis.[<a href="#cit/section_1.56">

130356</a>

1304]</li>

1305<li>

1306<strong>

1307Richter transformation.</strong>

1308 Patients who develop an aggressive high-grade non-Hodgkin lymphoma, usually diffuse large B-cell lymphoma, have a poor prognosis.[<a href="#cit/section_1.57">

130957</a>

1310]</li>

1311<li>

1312<strong>

1313Clearance of measurable residual disease (MRD).</strong>

1314 The improvements in response rates from more intensive regimens have maximized the clearance of MRD. In one prospective trial of 493 patients, clearance of MRD was an independent predictor of OS by multivariate analysis.[<a href="#cit/section_1.58">

131558</a>

1316] The surrogate end point of clearance of residual disease, while prognostic,[<a href="#cit/section_1.58">

131758</a>

1318,<a href="#cit/section_1.59">

131959</a>

1320] did not show improved survival in a randomized prospective trial. The necessary study would include patients who fail to completely clear the marrow with induction therapy and randomly assign them to further alternative treatment versus the same treatment later at relapse, looking at OS as the primary end point.[<a href="#cit/section_1.34">

132134</a>

1322,<a href="#cit/section_1.60">

132360</a>

1324]</li>

1325<li>

1326<strong>

1327CD38 immunophenotype.</strong>

1328[<a href="#cit/section_1.38">

132938</a>

1330,<a href="#cit/section_1.61">

133161</a>

1332] CD38 positivity (&gt;30%) correlates with a worse prognosis, but there is a 30% false-positive rate and a 50% false-negative rate using <em class="gene-name">

1333IgVH</em>

1334 mutational status as the gold standard for prognosis.</li>

1335<li>

1336<strong>

1337Other malignancies.</strong>

1338 Patients with CLL are also at increased risk of developing other malignancies, even before therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_1.62">

133962</a>

1340] A population-based analysis of almost 2 million cancer patients in the National Cancer Institute's Surveillance, Epidemiology, and End Results (SEER) Program database was performed. The findings suggested that cancer-specific survival for patients with pre-existing CLL who subsequently develop colorectal and breast cancer was significantly lower (hazard ratio [HR], 1.46; <em>

1341P</em>

1342 &lt; .001 for colorectal cancer and HR, 1.41; <em>

1343P </em>

1344= .005 for breast cancer) than cancer-specific survival for patients with colorectal and breast cancer who did not have antecedent CLL, after adjusting for age, sex, race, and disease stage, and excluding CLL-related deaths.[<a href="#cit/section_1.63">

134563</a>

1346]</li>

1347</ul>

1348</div>

1349<p id="_599" tabindex="-1">

1350An international prognostic index (IPI) for CLL (CLL-IPI) identified four prognostic subgroups on the basis of <em class="gene-name">

1351IgVH</em>

1352 mutational status, clinical stage, age (&#8804;65 years vs. &gt;65 years), and <em class="gene-name">

1353TP53</em>

1354 status (no abnormalities vs. del(17p) or <em class="gene-name">

1355TP53</em>

1356 mutation or both).[<a href="#cit/section_1.64">

135764</a>

1358] A scoring system to predict time to first treatment for early-stage CLL identified three adverse risk factors: unmutated <em class="gene-name">

1359IgVH</em>

1360, absolute lymphocyte count higher than 15 &#215; 10<span class="sup">

13619</span>

1362/L, and palpable lymph nodes.[<a href="#cit/section_1.65">

136365</a>

1364] Any new prognostic model, and even the commonly used CLL-IPI, may be outdated because of the use of highly effective frontline therapies, including BCL2 inhibitors and Bruton tyrosine kinase inhibitors.[<a href="#cit/section_1.66">

136566</a>

1366] Revalidation of these prognostic models will be required.</p>

1367</section>

1368<section id="_600">

1369<h3 id="_600_toc">

1370Follow-Up After Treatment</h3>

1371<p id="_601" tabindex="-1">

1372CT scans have a very limited role in monitoring patients after completion of treatment. CT scan or ultrasonography results determined the decision to treat for relapse in only 2 of 176 patients in three prospective trials for the German CLL Study Group.[<a href="#cit/section_1.67">

137367</a>

1374]</p>

1375</section>

1654 <section id="_7">

1655

1656 <h2>

1657Stage Information for CLL</h2>

1658

1659 <div id="_section_7" class="pdq-sections">

1660<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

1661<h6>

1662In This Section</h6>

1663<ul>

1664<li>

1665<a href="#_10_toc">

1666Rai Staging System</a>

1667</li>

1668<li>

1669<a href="#_21_toc">

1670Binet Classification</a>

1671</li>

1672</ul>

1673</nav>

1674<p id="_9" tabindex="-1">

1675Chronic lymphocytic leukemia (CLL) does not have a standard staging system. The Rai

1676staging system (<a href="/types/leukemia/hp/cll-treatment-pdq#_581">

1677Table 1</a>

1678) and the Binet classification (<a href="/types/leukemia/hp/cll-treatment-pdq#_582">

1679Table 2</a>

1680) are presented below.[<a href="#cit/section_2.1">

16811</a>

1682,<a href="#cit/section_2.2">

16832</a>

1684] A

1685National Cancer Institute (NCI)-sponsored working group has formulated standardized guidelines for

1686criteria related to eligibility, response, and toxic effects to be used in future clinical

1687trials in CLL.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

16883</a>

1689]</p>

1690<section id="_10">

1691<h3 id="_10_toc">

1692Rai Staging System</h3>

1693<table id="_581" class="table-default expandable-container">

1694<caption>

1695Table 1. Rai Staging System</caption>

1696<colgroup>

1697<col width="34.01%">

1698<col width="65.98%">

1699</colgroup>

1700<THead>

1701<tr>

1702<th align="Center" scope="col">

1703Stage</th>

1704<th align="Center" scope="col">

1705Stage Criteria</th>

1706</tr>

1707</THead>

1708<tbody>

1709<tr>

1710<td>

1711Stage 0</td>

1712<td>

1713Absolute lymphocytosis (&gt;15,000/mm<span class="sup">

17143</span>

1715) without adenopathy, hepatosplenomegaly, anemia, or thrombocytopenia.</td>

1716</tr>

1717<tr>

1718<td>

1719Stage I</td>

1720<td>

1721Absolute lymphocytosis with lymphadenopathy without hepatosplenomegaly, anemia, or thrombocytopenia.</td>

1722</tr>

1723<tr>

1724<td>

1725Stage II</td>

1726<td>

1727Absolute lymphocytosis with either hepatomegaly or splenomegaly with or without lymphadenopathy.</td>

1728</tr>

1729<tr>

1730<td>

1731Stage III</td>

1732<td>

1733Absolute lymphocytosis and anemia (hemoglobin &lt;11 g/dL) with or without lymphadenopathy, hepatomegaly, or splenomegaly.</td>

1734</tr>

1735<tr>

1736<td>

1737Stage IV</td>

1738<td>

1739Absolute lymphocytosis and thrombocytopenia (&lt;100,000/mm<span class="sup">

17403</span>

1741) with or without lymphadenopathy, hepatomegaly, splenomegaly, or anemia.</td>

1742</tr>

1743</tbody>

1744</table>

1745</section>

1746<section id="_21">

1747<h3 id="_21_toc">

1748Binet Classification</h3>

1749<table id="_582" class="table-default expandable-container">

1750<caption>

1751Table 2. Binet Classification System</caption>

1752<colgroup>

1753<col width="41.66%">

1754<col width="58.33%">

1755</colgroup>

1756<THead>

1757<tr>

1758<th align="Center" scope="col">

1759Stage</th>

1760<th align="Center" scope="col">

1761Stage Criteria</th>

1762</tr>

1763</THead>

1764<TFoot class="pdq-footer">

1765<tr>

1766<td colspan="2">

1767<span class="sup">

1768a</span>

1769Lymphoid areas include cervical, axillary, inguinal, and splenic.</td>

1770</tr>

1771</TFoot>

1772<tbody>

1773<tr>

1774<td>

1775Clinical stage A<span class="sup">

1776a</span>

1777</td>

1778<td>

1779No anemia or thrombocytopenia and fewer than three areas of lymphoid involvement (Rai stages 0, I, and II).</td>

1780</tr>

1781<tr>

1782<td>

1783Clinical stage B<span class="sup">

1784a</span>

1785</td>

1786<td>

1787No anemia or thrombocytopenia with three or more areas of lymphoid involvement (Rai stages I and II).</td>

1788</tr>

1789<tr>

1790<td>

1791Clinical stage C</td>

1792<td>

1793Anemia and/or thrombocytopenia regardless of the number of areas of lymphoid enlargement (Rai stages III and IV).</td>

1794</tr>

1795</tbody>

1796</table>

1797<p id="_29" tabindex="-1">

1798The Binet classification integrates the number of disease-involved nodal groups with bone marrow failure. Its major benefit derives from the

1799recognition of a predominantly splenic form of the disease, which may have a

1800better prognosis than was recognized in the Rai staging, and from the recognition that the

1801presence of anemia or thrombocytopenia has a similar prognosis and does not

1802merit a separate stage. Neither system separates immune from nonimmune causes

1803of cytopenia. Patients with thrombocytopenia, anemia, or both, which is caused by extensive marrow infiltration and impaired production (Rai III/IV, Binet C),

1804have a poorer prognosis than patients with immune cytopenias.[<a href="#cit/section_2.4">

18054</a>

1806]</p>

1807<p id="_604" tabindex="-1">

1808The

1809International Workshop on CLL has recommended

1810integrating the Rai and Binet systems as follows: A(0), A(I), A(II); B(I),

1811B(II); and C(III), C(IV).[<a href="#cit/section_2.5">

18125</a>

1813] The NCI-sponsored working

1814group has published guidelines for the diagnosis and treatment of CLL in both

1815clinical trial and general practice settings.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

18163</a>

1817] Use of these systems allows

1818comparison of clinical results and establishment of therapeutic guidelines.</p>

1819</section>

1849

1850 <section id="_30">

1851

1852 <h2>

1853Selection of Therapy for CLL</h2>

1854

1855 <div id="_section_30" class="pdq-sections">

1856<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

1857<h6>

1858In This Section</h6>

1859<ul>

1860<li>

1861<a href="#_791_toc">

1862Considerations for the Selection of Therapy</a>

1863</li>

1864<li>

1865<a href="#_609_toc">

1866Adverse Sequelae of the Disease and Therapy</a>

1867</li>

1868</ul>

1869</nav>

1870<p id="_596" tabindex="-1">

1871Treatment of patients with chronic lymphocytic leukemia (CLL) must be individualized on the basis of the clinical behavior of the disease.[<a href="#cit/section_3.1">

18721</a>

1873] Because this disease is generally not

1874curable, occurs in an older population, and often progresses slowly, it is

1875most often treated in a conservative fashion.[<a href="#cit/section_3.2">

18762</a>

1877] </p>

1878<p id="_632" tabindex="-1">

1879In older trials with data collected from the 1970s through the 1990s, the median survival for all patients ranged from 8 to 12 years.[<a href="#cit/section_3.3">

18803</a>

1881,<a href="#cit/section_3.4">

18824</a>

1883] However, with the introduction of the B-cell receptor inhibitors and targeting of BCL2, the median survival for all patients has not been reached with over 10 years of follow-up.</p>

1884<p id="_608" tabindex="-1">

1885Treatment of patients with CLL ranges from observation with treatment of infectious, hemorrhagic, or immunological

1886complications to a variety of therapeutic options administered as single agents or combination therapy. In asymptomatic patients, treatment may be deferred until the disease progresses and symptoms occur.[<a href="#cit/section_3.3">

18873</a>

1888] Because the rate of progression may vary from patient to patient, with long periods of stability and sometimes spontaneous regressions, frequent and careful observation is required to monitor the clinical course.[<a href="#cit/section_3.5">

18895</a>

1890] Although even asymptomatic patients with del(17p) on fluorescence <em>

1891in situ</em>

1892 hybridization (FISH) analysis (or <em class="gene-name">

1893TP53</em>

1894 mutation) may be followed with watchful waiting, frequent monitoring may be required to avert rapid progression. A meta-analysis of randomized

1895trials showed no survival benefit for immediate versus delayed therapy for

1896patients with early-stage disease.[<a href="#cit/section_3.6">

18976</a>

1898][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

1899Level of evidence A1</a>

1900] For patients with progressing CLL, treatment will not be curative in most cases. Selected patients treated with allogeneic stem cell transplantation

1901have achieved prolonged disease-free survival (DFS), sometimes exceeding 20 years.[<a href="#cit/section_3.7">

19027</a>

1903-<a href="#cit/section_3.11">

190411</a>

1905] Prolonged DFS was also noted in young patients (&lt;60 years) with <em class="gene-name">

1906IgVH</em>

1907 hypermutation who received the FCR regimen (fludarabine, cyclophosphamide, and rituximab).[<a href="#cit/section_3.12">

190812</a>

1909-<a href="#cit/section_3.14">

191014</a>

1911]</p>

1912<p id="_633" tabindex="-1">

1913The following clinical factors may be helpful in predicting progression of disease:[<a href="#cit/section_3.2">

19142</a>

1915]</p>

1916<div class="pdq-content-list">

1917<ul id="_634">

1918<li>

1919<em class="gene-name">

1920IgVH</em>

1921 gene mutation.</li>

1922<li>

1923Chromosomal abnormalities by FISH analysis or cytogenetics.</li>

1924<li>

1925Beta-2-microglobulin.</li>

1926<li>

1927Lymphocyte doubling time.</li>

1928</ul>

1929</div>

1930<p id="_788" tabindex="-1">

1931Symptomatic or progressive CLL is defined as the following by the International Workshop on Chronic Lymphocytic Leukemia:[<a href="#cit/section_3.15">

193215</a>

1933]</p>

1934<div class="pdq-content-list">

1935<ul id="_789">

1936<li>

1937Evidence of progressive marrow failure&#8212;the development or worsening of anemia and/or thrombocytopenia (in some patients, platelet counts &lt;100 &#215; 10<span class="sup">

19389</span>

1939/L may remain stable over a long period; this does not automatically require therapeutic intervention). Cutoff levels of hemoglobin less than 10 g/dL or platelet counts less than 50 &#215; 10<span class="sup">

19409</span>

1941/L are generally regarded as an indication for treatment. </li>

1942<li>

1943Massive (i.e., &#8805;6 cm below the left costal margin), progressive, or symptomatic splenomegaly.</li>

1944<li>

1945Massive nodes (i.e., &#8805;10 cm in longest diameter), progressive, or symptomatic lymphadenopathy.</li>

1946<li>

1947Progressive lymphocytosis with an increase of 50% or more over a 2-month period, or lymphocyte-doubling time (LDT) less than 6 months. LDT can be obtained by linear regression extrapolation of absolute lymphocyte counts obtained at intervals of 2 weeks over an observation period of 2 to 3 months; patients with initial blood lymphocyte counts less than 30 &#215; 10<span class="sup">

19489</span>

1949/L may require a longer observation period to determine the LDT. Factors contributing to lymphocytosis other than CLL (e.g., infections or steroid administration) should be excluded.</li>

1950<li>

1951Autoimmune complications, including anemia or thrombocytopenia that respond poorly to corticosteroids.</li>

1952<li>

1953Symptomatic or functional extranodal involvement (e.g., skin, kidney, lung, or spine).

1954

1955Disease-related symptoms defined as any of the following:

1956

1957<div class="pdq-content-list">

1958<ul id="_790">

1959<li>

1960Unintentional weight loss of 10% or more within the previous 6 months.</li>

1961<li>

1962Significant fatigue (i.e., Eastern Cooperative Oncology Group performance scale 2 or worse, cannot work, or unable to perform usual activities).</li>

1963<li>

1964Fevers of 100.5&#176;F or 38.0&#176;C or higher for 2 or more weeks without evidence of infection.</li>

1965<li>

1966Night sweats for at least 1 month without evidence of infection.</li>

1967</ul>

1968</div>

1969</li>

1970</ul>

1971</div>

1972<section id="_791">

1973<h3 id="_791_toc">

1974Considerations for the Selection of Therapy</h3>

1975<p id="_792" tabindex="-1">

1976The following general principles may provide a sequencing for available therapeutic options:</p>

1977<div class="pdq-content-list">

1978<ul id="_793">

1979<li>

1980 Despite many therapeutic options, asymptomatic or minimally affected patients with CLL are often offered observation outside the context of a clinical trial. Therapy often begins when patients develop profound cytopenias, or when symptoms, such as enlarging bulky lymphadenopathy or debilitating symptoms, substantially impact their quality of life.</li>

1981<li>

1982 Because nontransplant curative therapy has not been found, the initial goal of therapy is to maximize efficacy (with improvement of overall survival), while introducing the least overall short- and long-term toxicity.</li>

1983<li>

1984 The U.S. Food and Drug Administration approved the biological agents ibrutinib, acalabrutinib, and venetoclax for first-line use in newly diagnosed patients with CLL who require therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_3.16">

198516</a>

1986] In patients with adverse prognostic factors (especially del(17p) or mutated <em class="gene-name">

1987TP53</em>

1988), ibrutinib, acalabrutinib, or venetoclax should be considered.[<a href="#cit/section_3.17">

198917</a>

1990]</li>

1991<li>

1992Standard chemotherapeutic agents, such as fludarabine, bendamustine, cyclophosphamide, and chlorambucil, induce mutational damage to the genome that can manifest as more aggressive and refractory phenotypes upon relapse and can induce second malignancies. Yet, prolonged DFS (over 10 years) can be seen with the use of the FCR regimen in younger patients (&lt;60 years) with <em class="gene-name">

1993IgVH</em>

1994 hypermutation.[<a href="#cit/section_3.12">

199512</a>

1996-<a href="#cit/section_3.14">

199714</a>

1998]<div class="pdq-content-list">

1999<ul id="_794">

2000<li>

2001Avoiding alkylating agents and purine analogs also prevents prolonged cytopenias and the recurrent, long-lasting, and sometimes fatal infections seen after therapy with these agents.</li>

2002<li>

2003Avoiding chemotherapeutic agents up-front, when possible, is a new paradigm of sequencing therapy for CLL.</li>

2004</ul>

2005</div>

2006</li>

2007<li>

2008Older patients with comorbidities may better tolerate the newer biological agents (such as ibrutinib or venetoclax), monoclonal antibody therapy alone (such as high-dose rituximab), or dose modification of standard chemotherapeutic agents combined with rituximab. For older patients (&gt;65 years), the combination of rituximab plus bendamustine (BR regimen) resulted in fewer adverse events and better outcomes than the FCR regimen.[<a href="#cit/section_3.18">

200918</a>

2010]</li>

2011</ul>

2012</div>

2013</section>

2014<section id="_609">

2015<h3 id="_609_toc">

2016Adverse Sequelae of the Disease and Therapy</h3>

2017<p id="_33" tabindex="-1">

2018Infectious complications in advanced disease are in part a consequence of the

2019hypogammaglobulinemia and the inability to mount a humoral defense against

2020bacterial or viral agents. Herpes zoster represents a frequent viral infection

2021in these patients, but infections with <em>

2022Pneumocystis carinii</em>

2023 and <em>

2024Candida

2025albicans</em>

2026 may also occur. The early recognition of infections and the

2027institution of appropriate therapy are critical to the long-term survival of

2028these patients. A randomized study of intravenous immunoglobulin (400

2029mg/kg every 3 weeks for 1 year) in patients with CLL and

2030hypogammaglobulinemia produced significantly fewer bacterial infections and a

2031significant delay in onset of first infection during the study period.[<a href="#cit/section_3.19">

203219</a>

2033]

2034There was, however, no effect on survival. Routine chronic administration of

2035intravenous immunoglobulin is expensive, and the long-term benefit (&gt;1

2036year) is unproven.[<a href="#cit/section_3.20">

203720</a>

2038,<a href="#cit/section_3.21">

203921</a>

2040]</p>

2041<p id="_896" tabindex="-1">

2042Patients with CLL who required hospitalization for COVID-19 prior to the induction of vaccines fared poorly regardless of stage in two retrospective reports.[<a href="#cit/section_3.22">

204322</a>

2044,<a href="#cit/section_3.23">

204523</a>

2046] One of the studies noted a protective effect from Bruton tyrosine kinase (BTK) inhibitors (usually ibrutinib),[<a href="#cit/section_3.23">

204723</a>

2048] but this was not seen in the other report.[<a href="#cit/section_3.22">

204922</a>

2050] With enhanced testing and the advent of multiple therapeutic strategies to prevent and treat COVID-19, the case fatality rate for patients with CLL dropped from 35% in early 2020 to 11% in late 2020 and early 2021 (<em>

2051P</em>

2052 &lt; .001).[<a href="#cit/section_3.22">

205322</a>

2054] For patients requiring hospitalization, the case fatality rate dropped from 40% to 20% (<em>

2055P</em>

2056 = .003).</p>

2057<p id="_35" tabindex="-1">

2058Autoimmune hemolytic anemia and/or thrombocytopenia can occur in patients with

2059any stage of CLL.[<a href="#cit/section_3.24">

206024</a>

2061] Initial therapy involves corticosteroids with or without

2062alkylating agents (fludarabine can worsen the hemolytic anemia). It is

2063often necessary to control the autoimmune destruction with

2064corticosteroids, if possible, before administering marrow-suppressive

2065chemotherapy because it may be difficult for a patient to successfully

2066receive a red blood cell or platelet transfusion. Alternate therapies include

2067high-dose immune globulin, rituximab, cyclosporine, azathioprine, splenectomy, and low-dose radiation therapy to

2068the spleen.[<a href="#cit/section_3.3">

20693</a>

2070,<a href="#cit/section_3.25">

207125</a>

2072] Tumor lysis syndrome is an uncommon complication (presenting

2073in 1 of 300 patients) of chemotherapy for patients with bulky disease.[<a href="#cit/section_3.26">

207426</a>

2075]

2076</p>

2077<p id="_34" tabindex="-1">

2078Second malignancies and treatment-induced acute leukemias may also occur in a

2079small percentage of patients.[<a href="#cit/section_3.27">

208027</a>

2081] Transformation of CLL to diffuse large B-cell

2082lymphoma (Richter syndrome) occurs in 3% of CLL patients by 5 years. Richter's transformation carries a poor prognosis, with a median survival

2083of less than 1 year. However, 20% to 40% of patients may live more than 5 years

2084after aggressive combination chemotherapy, typically R-CHOP (rituximab, cyclophosphamide, doxorubicin, vincristine, and prednisone), often followed by autologous or allogeneic stem cell transplantation.[<a href="#cit/section_3.28">

208528</a>

2086-<a href="#cit/section_3.30">

208730</a>

2088] For more information, see

2089<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/b-cell-lymphoma-treatment-pdq">

2090B-Cell Non-Hodgkin Lymphoma Treatment</a>

2091.</p>

2092<p id="_897" tabindex="-1">

2093The BTK inhibitors increased the risk of bleeding requiring hospitalization (3-year risk for patients who received ibrutinib, 8.8% [95% confidence interval (CI), 6.5%&#8211;11.7%]) and atrial fibrillation (3-year incidence for patients who received ibrutinib, 22.7% [95% CI, 19.0%&#8211;26.6%]).[<a href="#cit/section_3.31">

209431</a>

2095] A randomized trial with a median follow-up of 41 months showed less atrial fibrillation for patients with CLL who received acalabrutinib compared with ibrutinib (9.4% vs. 16%; <em>

2096P</em>

2097 = .02).[<a href="#cit/section_3.32">

209832</a>

2099]</p>

2100</section>

2263<section id="_958">

2264<h3 id="_958_toc">

2265Treatment Options for Asymptomatic Chronic Lymphocytic Leukemia (CLL)</h3>

2266<section id="_959">

2267<h4 id="_959_toc">

2268Observation</h4>

2269<p id="_960" tabindex="-1">

2270Because of its indolent nature,

2271chemotherapy is not indicated for asymptomatic or minimally affected patients with CLL, and observation is the generally accepted approach.[<a href="#cit/section_4.1">

22721</a>

2273] Because the rate of progression may vary, with long periods of stability and sometimes spontaneous regressions, frequent and careful observation is required to monitor the clinical course.

2274One nomogram to predict time-to-first treatment relies on the number of lymph node sites, size of cervical lymph nodes, lactate dehydrogenase level, the <em class="gene-name">

2275IgVH</em>

2276 mutational status, and the presence of del(11q) or del(17p) established by fluorescence <em>

2277in situ</em>

2278 hybridization analysis.[<a href="#cit/section_4.2">

22792</a>

2280] Spontaneous regression, manifested by a sustained reduction of the malignant clone without therapy, occurs in less than 5% of patients. These patients almost exclusively have hypermutation of <em class="gene-name">

2281IgVH</em>

2282.[<a href="#cit/section_4.3">

22833</a>

2284]</p>

2285<p id="_961" tabindex="-1">

2286Evidence (observation):</p>

2287<div class="pdq-content-list">

2288<ol id="_962">

2289<li>

2290The French Cooperative Group on Chronic Lymphocytic Leukemia randomly assigned 1,535 patients with previously untreated stage A

2291disease to receive either chlorambucil or no immediate treatment.[<a href="#cit/section_4.4">

22924</a>

2293]<div class="pdq-content-list">

2294<ul id="_963">

2295<li>

2296The results showed no

2297survival advantage for immediate treatment with chlorambucil.[<a href="#cit/section_4.4">

22984</a>

2299][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

2300Level of evidence A1</a>

2301]</li>

2302</ul>

2303</div>

2304</li>

2305<li>

2306A meta-analysis evaluated six trials of patients with early-stage CLL that involved immediate versus deferred

2307therapy with chlorambucil (including the aforementioned trial by the French

2308Cooperative Group).[<a href="#cit/section_4.5">

23095</a>

2310]<div class="pdq-content-list">

2311<ul id="_964">

2312<li>

2313The results showed no difference in overall survival at 10

2314years.[<a href="#cit/section_4.5">

23155</a>

2316][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

2317Level of evidence A1</a>

2318]</li>

2319</ul>

2320</div>

2321</li>

2322</ol>

2323</div>

2324<p id="_965" tabindex="-1">

2325Despite many therapeutic options, observation should be considered for asymptomatic or minimally affected patients, even in the context of adverse prognostic findings. Therapy begins when patients develop profound cytopenias or when symptoms adversely impact quality of life.</p>

2326<p id="_966" tabindex="-1">

2327There are no clinical trial results that confirm that immediate treatment of asymptomatic or minimally affected patients with the B-cell receptor inhibitors or BCL2 inhibitors is superior to observation.</p>

2328<p id="_967" tabindex="-1">

2329Clinical trials will need to establish improved outcomes using the newer biological therapies in asymptomatic patients before observation or watchful waiting is discontinued.</p>

2330</section>

2331</section>

2337advanced clinical trial search</a>

2338 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

2339General information</a>

2436<section id="_909">

2437<h3 id="_909_toc">

2438Treatment Options for Symptomatic or Progressive Chronic Lymphocytic Leukemia (CLL)</h3>

2439<p id="_910" tabindex="-1">

2440The following regimens are considered first-line approaches for patients with CLL who are experiencing symptomatic progression: </p>

2441<div class="pdq-content-list">

2442<ul id="_911">

2443<li>

2444Acalabrutinib.</li>

2445<li>

2446Ibrutinib.</li>

2447<li>

2448Venetoclax with initial use of obinutuzumab or rituximab.</li>

2449<li>

2450Bendamustine and rituximab (BR).</li>

2451<li>

2452Fludarabine, cyclophosphamide, and rituximab (FCR).</li>

2453</ul>

2454</div>

2455<p id="_912" tabindex="-1">

2456Several large prospective clinical trials have compared these approaches. A chemotherapy-free approach for first-line therapy is usually preferred for most patients, but it is mandatory for patients with del(17p) or <em class="gene-name">

2457TP53</em>

2458-positive disease.[<a href="#cit/section_5.1">

24591</a>

2460-<a href="#cit/section_5.5">

24615</a>

2462]</p>

2463<section id="_994">

2464<h4 id="_994_toc">

2465Ibrutinib versus FCR</h4>

2466<p id="_1047" tabindex="-1">

2467Ibrutinib is a selective irreversible inhibitor of Bruton tyrosine kinase (BTK), a signaling molecule located upstream in the B-cell receptor-signaling cascade.</p>

2468<p id="_1051" tabindex="-1">

2469Evidence (ibrutinib vs. FCR):</p>

2470<div class="pdq-content-list">

2471<ol id="_1018">

2472<li>

2473<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02048813">

2474ECOG-E1912</a>

2475 (NCT02048813) was a prospective randomized trial that compared ibrutinib and rituximab with FCR. A total of 529 patients previously untreated for CLL were randomly assigned in a 2:1 ratio to receive either ibrutinib and rituximab followed by ibrutinib maintenance (354 patients) or six cycles of FCR (175 patients).[<a href="#cit/section_5.6">

24766</a>

2477,<a href="#cit/section_5.7">

24787</a>

2479]<div class="pdq-content-list">

2480<ul id="_1020">

2481<li>

2482With a median follow-up of 5.8 years, the 5-year overall survival (OS) rate favored the ibrutinib arm (95% vs. 89%) (hazard ratio [HR], 0.47; 95% confidence interval [CI], 0.25&#8211;0.89; <em>

2483P</em>

2484 = .018).[<a href="#cit/section_5.7">

24857</a>

2486][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

2487Level of evidence A1</a>

2488]</li>

2489<li>

2490For the 281 patients with <em class="gene-name">

2491IgVH</em>

2492-unmutated disease, the 5-year progression-free survival (PFS) rate favored ibrutinib plus rituximab versus FCR (75% vs. 33%) (HR, 0.27; 95% CI, 0.18&#8722;0.41; <em>

2493P</em>

2494 &lt; .0001). For the 114 patients with <em class="gene-name">

2495IgVH</em>

2496-mutated disease, the 5-year PFS rate was also significantly different, at 83% for the ibrutinib arm and 68% for the FCR arm (HR, 0.27; 95% CI, 0.11&#8722;0.62; <em>

2497P</em>

2498 = .001).[<a href="#cit/section_5.6">

24996</a>

2500-<a href="#cit/section_5.8">

25018</a>

2502] </li>

2503<li>

2504Although undetectable measurable residual disease (MRD) was less than 10% between 12 and 36 months follow-up, patients with detectable MRD did not have significantly worse PFS (<em>

2505P</em>

2506 = .14 at 12 months, .90 at 24 months, and .53 at 36 months).[<a href="#cit/section_5.9">

25079</a>

2508]</li>

2509</ul>

2510</div>

2511</li>

2512</ol>

2513</div>

2514</section>

2515<section id="_1021">

2516<h4 id="_1021_toc">

2517Ibrutinib versus ibrutinib plus rituximab versus BR</h4>

2518<p id="_1052" tabindex="-1">

2519Evidence (ibrutinib vs. ibrutinib plus rituximab vs. BR):</p>

2520<div class="pdq-content-list">

2521<ol id="_1022">

2522<li>

2523A prospective trial included 547 previously untreated patients aged 65 years or older. Patients were randomly assigned to receive BR, ibrutinib alone, or ibrutinib plus rituximab.[<a href="#cit/section_5.10">

252410</a>

2525]<div class="pdq-content-list">

2526<ul id="_918">

2527<li>

2528With a median follow-up of 38 months, the 2-year PFS rate was 74% for patients who received BR. The rates were significantly higher for patients who received ibrutinib alone (87%; HR, 0.39; 95% CI, 0.25&#8211;0.58) or ibrutinib plus rituximab (88%; HR, 0.38; 95% CI, 0.25&#8211;0.59; <em>

2529P</em>

2530 &lt; .001).[<a href="#cit/section_5.10">

253110</a>

2532][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

2533Level of evidence B1</a>

2534]</li>

2535<li>

2536There was no difference in PFS between the two ibrutinib groups (HR, 1.00; 95% CI, 0.62&#8211;1.62; <em>

2537P</em>

2538 = .49) and no difference in OS between each of the groups.</li>

2539</ul>

2540</div>

2541</li>

2542</ol>

2543</div>

2544</section>

2545<section id="_1023">

2546<h4 id="_1023_toc">

2547Ibrutinib versus acalabrutinib</h4>

2548<p id="_1053" tabindex="-1">

2549Evidence (ibrutinib vs. acalabrutinib):</p>

2550<div class="pdq-content-list">

2551<ol id="_1024">

2552<li>

2553A prospective randomized trial of 533 previously untreated patients compared the BTK inhibitors acalabrutinib and ibrutinib.[<a href="#cit/section_5.11">

255411</a>

2555]<div class="pdq-content-list">

2556<ul id="_919">

2557<li>

2558With a median follow-up of 41 months, acalabrutinib was noninferior to ibrutinib, with a median PFS of 38.4 months for patients in both arms of the trial (HR, 1.00; 95% CI, 0.79&#8211;1.27).[<a href="#cit/section_5.11">

255911</a>

2560][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

2561Level of evidence B1</a>

2562]</li>

2563<li>

2564The incidence of atrial fibrillation of any grade was lower for patients who received acalabrutinib than for patients who received ibrutinib (9.4% vs. 16.0%, <em>

2565P</em>

2566 = .02).</li>

2567</ul>

2568</div>

2569</li>

2570</ol>

2571</div>

2572</section>

2573<section id="_1025">

2574<h4 id="_1025_toc">

2575Ibrutinib versus rituximab plus ibrutinib</h4>

2576<p id="_1054" tabindex="-1">

2577Evidence (ibrutinib vs. rituximab plus ibrutinib):</p>

2578<div class="pdq-content-list">

2579<ol id="_1026">

2580<li>

2581A prospective randomized trial included 208 patients who were previously untreated or had relapsed disease. Patients received rituximab plus ibrutinib or ibrutinib alone.[<a href="#cit/section_5.12">

258212</a>

2583]<div class="pdq-content-list">

2584<ul id="_920">

2585<li>

2586With a median follow-up of 36 months, there was no difference in PFS (86%; HR, 1.04; 95% CI, 0.49&#8722;2.20; <em>

2587P</em>

2588 = .91).[<a href="#cit/section_5.12">

258912</a>

2590][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

2591Level of evidence B1</a>

2592]</li>

2593</ul>

2594</div>

2595</li>

2596</ol>

2597</div>

2598</section>

2599<section id="_1027">

2600<h4 id="_1027_toc">

2601Venetoclax plus obinutuzumab versus chlorambucil plus obinutuzumab</h4>

2602<p id="_1055" tabindex="-1">

2603Evidence (venetoclax plus obinutuzumab vs. chlorambucil plus obinutuzumab):</p>

2604<div class="pdq-content-list">

2605<ol id="_1028">

2606<li>

2607The prospective <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02242942">

2608CLL14</a>

2609 trial (NCT02242942) included 432 previously untreated patients with significant medical comorbidities (6 or higher on the Cumulative Illness Rating Scale; median age, 72 years). Patients were randomly assigned to receive venetoclax (a highly selective inhibitor of BCL2) plus obinutuzumab (the human anti-CD20 monoclonal antibody) versus chlorambucil plus obinutuzumab.[<a href="#cit/section_5.13">

261013</a>

2611]<div class="pdq-content-list">

2612<ul id="_921">

2613<li>

2614With a median follow-up of 28.1 months, the 2-year PFS rate was significantly higher for patients who received venetoclax plus obinutuzumab at 88.2% (95% CI, 83.7%&#8211;92.6%), compared with 64.1% for patients who received chlorambucil plus obinutuzumab (95% CI, 57.4%&#8211;70.8%) (HR, 0.35; 95% CI, 0.23&#8211;0.53; <em>

2615P</em>

2616 &lt; .001).[<a href="#cit/section_5.13">

261713</a>

2618][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

2619Level of evidence B1</a>

2620]</li>

2621<li>

2622With a median follow-up of 52.4 months, the 4-year PFS rate for the venetoclax arm was 74.0% with 57% undetectable (&lt;10 <span class="sup">

2623-4</span>

2624) MRD in the bone marrow at 3 years versus a 35.4% 4-year PFS rate and 17% MRD-negative marrow in the chlorambucil arm at 3 years (HR, 0.33; 95% CI, 0.25&#8722;0.45; <em>

2625P</em>

2626 &lt; .0001).[<a href="#cit/section_5.14">

262714</a>

2628,<a href="#cit/section_5.15">

262915</a>

2630][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

2631Level of evidence B1</a>

2632]</li>

2633</ul>

2634</div>

2635</li>

2636</ol>

2637</div>

2638</section>

2639<section id="_1029">

2640<h4 id="_1029_toc">

2641Venetoclax plus rituximab (VenR) versus BR</h4>

2642<p id="_1056" tabindex="-1">

2643Evidence (VenR vs. BR):</p>

2644<div class="pdq-content-list">

2645<ol id="_1030">

2646<li>

2647The prospective <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02005471">

2648MURANO</a>

2649 trial (NCT02005471) included 389 patients with relapsed or refractory CLL. Patients were randomly assigned to receive VenR (venetoclax for 2 years plus rituximab for the first 6 months) versus 6 months of BR.<div class="pdq-content-list">

2650<ul id="_922">

2651<li>

2652With a median follow-up of 24 months, the 2-year PFS rate was 84.9% for VenR and 36.3% for BR (HR, 0.17; 95% CI, 0.11&#8211;0.25; <em>

2653P</em>

2654 &lt; .001).[<a href="#cit/section_5.16">

265516</a>

2656,<a href="#cit/section_5.17">

265717</a>

2658] An update with a 48-month median follow-up, reported in abstract form, showed a 4-year OS rate of 85.3% for VenR and 66.8% for BR (HR, 0.41; 95% CI, 0.26&#8722;0.65; <em>

2659P</em>

2660 &lt; .0001).[<a href="#cit/section_5.18">

266118</a>

2662][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

2663Level of evidence A1</a>

2664]</li>

2665<li>

2666With a median follow-up of 59.2 months, the 5-year OS was 82.1% (76.4%&#8211;87.8%) for patients who received VenR and 62.2% (54.8%&#8211;69.6%) for patients who received BR (<em>

2667P</em>

2668 &lt; .0001).[<a href="#cit/section_5.19">

266919</a>

2670][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

2671Level of evidence A1</a>

2672] The median time to next treatment was 57.8 months (55.1&#8211;not estimable) for VenR.</li>

2673<li>

2674For the 43% of patients assigned to VenR who achieved undetectable MRD at the end of treatment, the median time to MRD conversion was 19.4 months. The median time from MRD conversion to overt clinical progressive disease was another 25.2 months.[<a href="#cit/section_5.19">

267519</a>

2676]</li>

2677</ul>

2678</div>

2679</li>

2680</ol>

2681</div>

2682</section>

2683<section id="_1031">

2684<h4 id="_1031_toc">

2685Acalabrutinib plus obinutuzumab versus acalabrutinib versus chlorambucil plus obinutuzumab</h4>

2686<p id="_1048" tabindex="-1">

2687Acalabrutinib is a highly selective covalent irreversible BTK inhibitor, designed to minimize the gastrointestinal toxicities and risk of atrial fibrillation seen with ibrutinib.</p>

2688<p id="_1057" tabindex="-1">

2689 Evidence (acalabrutinib plus obinutuzumab vs. acalabrutinib vs. chlorambucil plus obinutuzumab):</p>

2690<div class="pdq-content-list">

2691<ol id="_1032">

2692<li>

2693The prospective <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02475681">

2694ELEVATE TN</a>

2695 trial (NCT02475681) included 535 previously untreated patients aged 65 years or older with comorbidities (e.g., creatinine clearance &lt;70 mL/min). Patients were randomly assigned to one of three arms: acalabrutinib plus obinutuzumab, acalabrutinib alone, or chlorambucil plus obinutuzumab.[<a href="#cit/section_5.20">

269620</a>

2697] <div class="pdq-content-list">

2698<ul id="_923">

2699<li>

2700With a median follow-up of 28 months, the 24-month PFS rates were 93% for acalabrutinib plus obinutuzumab (HR, 0.10; 95% CI, 0.06&#8722;0.17; <em>

2701P</em>

2702 &lt; .0001), 87% for acalabrutinib alone (HR, 0.20; 95% CI, 0.13&#8722;0.30; <em>

2703P</em>

2704 &lt; .0001), and 47% for chlorambucil plus obinutuzumab.[<a href="#cit/section_5.20">

270520</a>

2706][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

2707Level of evidence B1</a>

2708]</li>

2709<li>

2710There was a small but significant difference in the PFS rates between the two acalabrutinib groups (93% vs. 87% at 24 months), which favored the combination (HR, 0.49; 95% CI, 0.26&#8722;0.95).[<a href="#cit/section_5.20">

271120</a>

2712]</li>

2713</ul>

2714</div>

2715</li>

2716</ol>

2717</div>

2718</section>

2719<section id="_1033">

2720<h4 id="_1033_toc">

2721Zanubrutinib versus BR</h4>

2722<p id="_1058" tabindex="-1">

2723Evidence (zanubrutinib vs. BR):</p>

2724<div class="pdq-content-list">

2725<ol id="_1034">

2726<li>

2727A prospective trial included 590 previously untreated patients aged 65 years or older. Patients were randomly assigned to receive zanubrutinib or BR.[<a href="#cit/section_5.21">

272821</a>

2729]<div class="pdq-content-list">

2730<ul id="_1002">

2731<li>

2732With a median follow-up of 26.2 months, the 2-year PFS rate was 85.5% (80.1%&#8211;89.6%) for patients who received zanubrutinib and 69.5% (62.4%&#8211;75.5%) for patients who received BR (HR, 0.42; 95% CI, 0.28&#8211;0.63; <em>

2733P</em>

2734 &lt; .0001).[<a href="#cit/section_5.21">

273521</a>

2736][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

2737Level of evidence B1</a>

2738]</li>

2739</ul>

2740</div>

2741</li>

2742</ol>

2743</div>

2744</section>

2745<section id="_1035">

2746<h4 id="_1035_toc">

2747BR versus FCR</h4>

2748<p id="_1059" tabindex="-1">

2749Evidence (BR vs. FCR):</p>

2750<div class="pdq-content-list">

2751<ol id="_1036">

2752<li>

2753The German CLL Study Group compared BR versus FCR as first-line therapy in patients with CLL who required therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_5.22">

275422</a>

2755]<div class="pdq-content-list">

2756<ul id="_924">

2757<li>

2758 With a median follow-up of 37.1 months, the median PFS was better for patients who received FCR (55.2 months vs. 41.7 months) (HR, 1.64; 90% CI, 1.31&#8211;2.06; <em>

2759P</em>

2760 = .001), but there was no difference in the OS rate at 3 years (91% vs. 92%, not significant).[<a href="#cit/section_5.22">

276122</a>

2762][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

2763Level of evidence B1</a>

2764]</li>

2765<li>

2766In patients older than 65 years, there was no difference in PFS between the two arms, but more infections occurred with FCR than with BR (grade 3 to 5 infection, 47% vs. 27%).</li>

2767</ul>

2768</div>

2769</li>

2770</ol>

2771</div>

2772</section>

2773<section id="_1037">

2774<h4 id="_1037_toc">

2775FCR</h4>

2776<p id="_1049" tabindex="-1">

2777FCR is used for patients with an <em class="gene-name">

2778IgVH</em>

2779 hypermutation. </p>

2780<p id="_1060" tabindex="-1">

2781Evidence (FCR):</p>

2782<div class="pdq-content-list">

2783<ol id="_1038">

2784<li>

2785Several trials used FCR for appropriate patients with mutated <em class="gene-name">

2786IgVH</em>

2787 who required therapy. <div class="pdq-content-list">

2788<ul id="_1050">

2789<li>

2790The PFS rate exceeded 60% at more than 10 years.[<a href="#cit/section_5.23">

279123</a>

2792-<a href="#cit/section_5.25">

279325</a>

2794][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

2795Level of evidence C2</a>

2796] Nonetheless, late relapses were seen beyond 10 years.</li>

2797</ul>

2798</div>

2799</li>

2800</ol>

2801</div>

2802</section>

2803<section id="_1039">

2804<h4 id="_1039_toc">

2805Ibrutinib plus venetoclax</h4>

2806<p id="_1061" tabindex="-1">

2807Evidence (ibrutinib plus venetoclax):</p>

2808<div class="pdq-content-list">

2809<ol id="_1040">

2810<li>

2811A phase II trial included 80 previously untreated patients who were aged 65 or older or had high-risk disease. Patients were treated with ibrutinib for 3 months followed by combined ibrutinib plus venetoclax for a total of 24 months.[<a href="#cit/section_5.26">

281226</a>

2813]<div class="pdq-content-list">

2814<ul id="_925">

2815<li>

2816The 1-year response rate was 88%, the PFS rate was 98% (95% CI, 94%&#8211;100%), and the OS rate was 99% (95% CI, 96%&#8211;100%).[<a href="#cit/section_5.26">

281726</a>

2818][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

2819Level of evidence C3</a>

2820]</li>

2821<li>

2822The toxicity of the combination is similar to either agent alone and avoids the tumor lysis syndrome seen when starting with venetoclax.</li>

2823<li>

2824High rates of undetectable MRD (&lt;10<span class="sup">

2825-4</span>

2826 by 8 color flow cytometry) in the peripheral blood (75%) and bone marrow (72%) is unprecedented. The clinical significance of this finding awaits prospective randomized trials to establish clinical outcomes versus either drug alone. This combination has also been tested in the relapsed/refractory setting.[<a href="#cit/section_5.27">

282727</a>

2828]</li>

2829</ul>

2830</div>

2831</li>

2832</ol>

2833</div>

2834</section>

2835<p id="_926" tabindex="-1">

2836In summary, these trials establish the use of venetoclax with obinutuzumab or rituximab, or the use of ibrutinib or acalabrutinib as first-line therapy in previously untreated patients with CLL. A lower rate of atrial fibrillation may favor the use of acalabrutinib over ibrutinib. Unlike ibrutinib or acalabrutinib, which are given continuously until relapse, venetoclax may be stopped after 12 months, with durable maintenance of remission. Venetoclax, ibrutinib, or acalabrutinib can be readministered with success, if needed. The combination of venetoclax and ibrutinib or acalabrutinib or zanubrutinib with or without obinutuzumab needs to be evaluated in prospective randomized trials versus the use of these agents alone with or without obinutuzumab. Several provocative phase II trials with these combinations have resulted in unprecedented rates of MRD-negative disease which appear more durable;[<a href="#cit/section_5.26">

283726</a>

2838,<a href="#cit/section_5.28">

283928</a>

2840-<a href="#cit/section_5.31">

284131</a>

2842] whether this results in any clinical advantage to a more sequential approach requires prospective randomized trials. The considerable financial toxicity of this combination mandates verification of superior efficacy. These trials further establish the rationale for a chemotherapy-free approach for first-line therapy for CLL instead of the previous standard of BR and FCR (which proved more efficacious than chlorambucil regimens).</p>

2843</section>

2850 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

2959[PUBMED Abstract]</a>

2960</li>

Lancet Haematol 8 (12): e879-e890, 2021.&#160;<a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=34826411&amp;dopt=Abstract" title="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=34826411&amp;dopt=Abstract">

2986 <h2>

2987Treatment of Recurrent or Refractory CLL</h2>

2988

2989 <div id="_section_101" class="pdq-sections">
