3034<section id="_927">

3035<h3 id="_927_toc">

3036Treatment Options for Recurrent or Refractory Chronic Lymphocytic Leukemia (CLL)</h3>

3037<p id="_928" tabindex="-1">

3038The same regimens considered for first-line therapy for patients with CLL can be readministered in a sequential fashion. These regimens are described in more detail under first-line therapy. For more information, see the <a href="/types/leukemia/hp/cll-treatment-pdq#_613">

3039Treatment of Symptomatic or Progressive CLL</a>

3040 section.</p>

3041<div class="pdq-content-list">

3042<ul id="_929">

3043<li>

3044Ibrutinib with or without rituximab or obinutuzumab.</li>

3045<li>

3046Venetoclax with or without rituximab or obinutuzumab.</li>

3047<li>

3048Acalabrutinib with or without rituximab or obinutuzumab.</li>

3049<li>

3050Bendamustine plus rituximab (BR).</li>

3051<li>

3052Fludarabine, cyclophosphamide, and rituximab (FCR).</li>

3053</ul>

3054</div>

3055<p id="_930" tabindex="-1">

3056In the relapsed setting, venetoclax showed similar efficacy and safety even after previous therapy with ibrutinib or idelalisib (the phosphatidylinositol 3-kinase [PI3K] delta inhibitor).[<a href="#cit/section_6.1">

30571</a>

3058,<a href="#cit/section_6.2">

30592</a>

3060]</p>

3061<p id="_931" tabindex="-1">

3062Similarly, in a trial reported in abstract form, ibrutinib and acalabrutinib showed similar efficacy and safety after previous therapy with venetoclax.[<a href="#cit/section_6.3">

30633</a>

3064] Sequencing these novel agents showed efficacy in the relapsed/refractory setting.[<a href="#cit/section_6.4">

30654</a>

3066]</p>

3067<section id="_932">

3068<h4 id="_932_toc">

3069Chimeric antigen receptor (CAR) T-cell therapy</h4>

3070<p id="_933" tabindex="-1">

3071Autologous T cells can be modified by viral vectors to incorporate antigen receptor specificity for the B-cell antigen CD19 and then infused into previously treated patients.[<a href="#cit/section_6.5">

30725</a>

3073] A dramatic response lasting 6 months has prompted larger trials of this concept. Ongoing clinical trials are testing the concept of T cells directed at CD19 with engineered CAR T cells.[<a href="#cit/section_6.6">

30746</a>

3075-<a href="#cit/section_6.8">

30768</a>

3077]</p>

3078</section>

3079<section id="_934">

3080<h4 id="_934_toc">

3081PI3K inhibitors</h4>

3082<p id="_935" tabindex="-1">

3083Idelalisib is an oral inhibitor of the delta isoform of PI3K, which is in the B-cell receptor-signaling cascade. This drug has been withdrawn from its U.S. Food and Drug Administration indication due to toxicity and is no longer available. Duvelisib is an oral dual inhibitor of the delta and gamma isoforms of PI3K.[<a href="#cit/section_6.9">

30849</a>

3085]</p>

3086<div class="pdq-content-list">

3087<ol id="_936">

3088<li>

3089In a prospective trial, 319 patients with relapsed and refractory CLL/small lymphocytic lymphoma were randomly assigned to receive duvelisib versus ofatumumab.[<a href="#cit/section_6.10">

309010</a>

3091]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3092<ul id="_938">

3093<li>

3094With a median follow-up of 24 months, the median PFS was significantly higher for patients who received duvelisib, at 13.3 months, than for patients who received ofatumumab, at 9.9 months (HR, 0.52; <em>

3095P</em>

3096 &lt; .0001).</li>

3097</ul>

3098</div>

3099</li>

3100</ol>

3101</div>

3102</section>

3103<section id="_940">

3104<h4 id="_940_toc">

3105Lenalidomide</h4>

3106<p id="_941" tabindex="-1">

3107Lenalidomide is an oral immunomodulatory agent with response rates of more than 50%, with or without rituximab, for patients with previously treated and untreated disease.[<a href="#cit/section_6.11">

310811</a>

3109-<a href="#cit/section_6.17">

311017</a>

3111][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3112Level of evidence C3</a>

3113] Prolonged, lower-dose approaches and attention to prevention of tumor lysis syndrome are suggested with this agent.[<a href="#cit/section_6.11">

311411</a>

3115,<a href="#cit/section_6.18">

311618</a>

3117] Combination therapy and long-term toxicities from using lenalidomide (such as increased myelodysplasia, as seen in myeloma patients) remain undefined for patients with CLL.</p>

3118</section>

3119<section id="_942">

3120<h4 id="_942_toc">

3121Bone marrow or peripheral blood stem cell transplantation</h4>

3122<p id="_943" tabindex="-1">

3123In a prospective randomized trial, 241 previously untreated patients younger than 66 years with advanced-stage disease received induction therapy with a CHOP (cyclophosphamide, doxorubicin, vincristine, and prednisone)-based regimen followed by fludarabine.[<a href="#cit/section_6.19">

312419</a>

3125] Complete responders (105 patients) were randomly assigned to undergo autologous stem cell transplantation (SCT) or observation, while the other 136 patients were randomly assigned to receive dexamethasone, high-dose cytarabine, and cisplatin reinduction followed by either autologous SCT or fludarabine plus cyclophosphamide (FC). Although the 3-year event-free survival (EFS) favored autologous SCT in complete responders, there was no difference in OS in any of the randomized comparisons.[<a href="#cit/section_6.19">

312619</a>

3127][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3128Level of evidence B1</a>

3129] Autologous bone marrow/stem cell transplantation is rarely employed for patients with relapsed CLL.</p>

3130<p id="_944" tabindex="-1">

3131Patients with adverse prognostic factors are very likely to die from CLL. These patients are candidates for clinical trials that employ high-dose chemotherapy and immunotherapy with myeloablative or nonmyeloablative allogeneic peripheral blood SCT.[<a href="#cit/section_6.20">

313220</a>

3133-<a href="#cit/section_6.25">

313425</a>

3135] Although most patients who attain complete remission after autologous SCT eventually relapse, a survival plateau for allogeneic SCT suggests an additional graft-versus-leukemia effect.[<a href="#cit/section_6.25">

313625</a>

3137] A series (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00281983">

3138NCT00281983</a>

3139) of 90 patients with relapsed or refractory CLL who underwent allogeneic SCT reported a 6-year OS rate of 58% and a 6-year EFS rate of 38%, which included patients with the worst prognostic factors (such as <em class="gene-name">

3140TP53</em>

3141 gene mutation).[<a href="#cit/section_6.26">

314226</a>

3143][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3144Level of evidence C2</a>

3145] </p>

3146</section>

3147<section id="_945">

3148<h4 id="_945_toc">

3149Ofatumumab</h4>

3150<p id="_946" tabindex="-1">

3151Ofatumumab is a humanized anti-CD20 monoclonal antibody.</p>

3152<p id="_947" tabindex="-1">

3153Evidence (ofatumumab alone and in combination with chlorambucil):</p>

3154<div class="pdq-content-list">

3155<ol id="_948">

3156<li>

3157A prospective trial included 474 previously treated patients who attained partial or complete remission to second- or third-line chemotherapy. Patients were randomly assigned to 2 years of maintenance therapy with ofatumumab versus observation.[<a href="#cit/section_6.27">

315827</a>

3159]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3160<ul id="_949">

3161<li>

3162With a median follow-up of 19 months, median PFS favored the ofatumumab maintenance arm, at 29.4 months versus 15.2 months (HR, 0.50; 95% CI, 0.38&#8211;0.66; <em>

3163P</em>

3164 &lt; .0001). There was no difference in OS.[<a href="#cit/section_6.27">

316527</a>

3166][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3167Level of evidence B1</a>

3168]</li>

3169</ul>

3170</div>

3171</li>

3172<li>

3173A prospective randomized trial of 447 patients who were previously untreated compared ofatumumab plus chlorambucil with chlorambucil alone.[<a href="#cit/section_6.28">

317428</a>

3175]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3176<ul id="_950">

3177<li>

3178 With a median follow-up of 2 years, median PFS favored the ofatumumab plus chlorambucil arm, at 22.4 months versus 13.1 months (HR, 0.57; 95% CI, 0.45&#8211;0.72; <em>

3179P</em>

3180 = .0001). There was no difference in OS.[<a href="#cit/section_6.28">

318128</a>

3182][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3183Level of evidence B1</a>

3184]</li>

3185</ul>

3186</div>

3187</li>

3188</ol>

3189</div>

3190</section>

3191<section id="_951">

3192<h4 id="_951_toc">

3193Involved-field radiation therapy</h4>

3194<p id="_952" tabindex="-1">

3195Relatively low doses of radiation therapy can be administered for lymphadenopathy that causes problems due to size or encroachment on adjacent organs. Sometimes radiation therapy to one

3196nodal area or the spleen will result in an abscopal effect (i.e., the shrinkage of lymph

3197nodes in untreated sites).</p>

3198</section>

3199<section id="_953">

3200<h4 id="_953_toc">

3201Alemtuzumab</h4>

3202<p id="_954" tabindex="-1">

3203Alemtuzumab is no longer available commercially in the United States for neoplastic indications but can be obtained from the pharmaceutical company on a compassionate-use basis (<a href="https://www.lemtradarems.com/" title="https://www.lemtradarems.com/">

3204Lemtrada REMS [Risk Evaluation and Mitigation Strategy] Program</a>

3205).</p>

3206<p id="_955" tabindex="-1">

3207Alemtuzumab, the monoclonal antibody directed at CD52, shows activity in the setting of chemotherapy-resistant disease or high-risk untreated patients with del(17p) or <em class="gene-name">

3208TP53</em>

3209 mutations.[<a href="#cit/section_6.29">

321029</a>

3211-<a href="#cit/section_6.31">

321231</a>

3213] As a single agent, the subcutaneous route of delivery is preferred to the intravenous route in patients because of the similar efficacy and decreased adverse effects, including less acute allergic reactions that were shown in some nonrandomized reports.[<a href="#cit/section_6.31">

321431</a>

3215-<a href="#cit/section_6.35">

321635</a>

3217]</p>

3218<p id="_956" tabindex="-1">

3219In a combination regimen, subcutaneous alemtuzumab plus fludarabine (with or without cyclophosphamide) or intravenous alemtuzumab plus alkylating agents have resulted in excess infectious toxicities and death, with no compensatory improvement in efficacy in three phase II trials and one randomized trial.[<a href="#cit/section_6.36">

322036</a>

3221-<a href="#cit/section_6.38">

322238</a>

3223][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3224Level of evidence C3</a>

3225]; [<a href="#cit/section_6.39">

322639</a>

3227][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3228Level of evidence B1</a>

3229]</p>

3230</section>

3231</section>

3232<section id="_TrialSearch_101_sid_6">

3233<h3 id="_TrialSearch_101_sid_6_toc">

3234Current Clinical Trials</h3>

3235<p id="_TrialSearch_101_22" tabindex="-1">

3236Use our <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced">

3237advanced clinical trial search</a>

3238 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

3239General information</a>

3240 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

3404 <section id="_1006">

3405

3406 <h2>

3407MRD Testing Outside the Context of a Clinical Trial</h2>

3408

3409 <div id="_section_1006" class="pdq-sections">

3410<p id="_1007" tabindex="-1">

3411Undetectable measurable residual disease (MRD) (&#8804;1 &#215; 10<span class="sup">

3412-4</span>

3413 chronic lymphocytic leukemia [CLL] cells in peripheral blood or bone marrow aspirates) can be confirmed by flow cytometry or next-generation sequencing. The attainment of undetectable MRD represents an even more stringent complete remission that was prognostic for improved progression-free survival (PFS) and overall survival (OS) in multiple studies.[<a href="#cit/section_7.1">

34141</a>

3415-<a href="#cit/section_7.4">

34164</a>

3417]</p>

3418<p id="_1008" tabindex="-1">

3419Testing for undetectable MRD has become a standard parameter for defining responses in all modern clinical trials for CLL. Undetectable MRD has prognostic value but its status as a predictive marker is uncertain. The potential value of MRD testing in routine clinical practice depends on whether it can be used for clinical decision making such as stopping, changing, or continuing treatment. High-level evidence for this intervention would require a prospective randomized clinical trial in which MRD was used as a predictive biomarker for a group attaining an OS advantage compared with a control group disregarding MRD status. Such evidence has not been attained. Similar to outcomes in follicular lymphoma and other indolent lymphoid neoplasms, improved PFS in patients with CLL does not directly predict OS.</p>

3420<p id="_1009" tabindex="-1">

3421The use of time-limited therapy is not as valuable in routine clinical practice. The use of time-limited therapy with venetoclax or the investigational combination of venetoclax and a Bruton tyrosine kinase inhibitor has produced complete responses, and even undetectable MRD, in most patients.[<a href="#cit/section_7.1">

34221</a>

3423,<a href="#cit/section_7.2">

34242</a>

3425,<a href="#cit/section_7.5">

34265</a>

3427]</p>

3428<p id="_1010" tabindex="-1">

3429A phase II trial used a combination of venetoclax and ibrutinib in patients with undetectable MRD after 1 year of therapy. Patients were randomly assigned to receive either ibrutinib maintenance therapy or treatment cessation.[<a href="#cit/section_7.5">

34305</a>

3431] All MRD-positive patients continued to receive ibrutinib. With a median follow-up of 34.4 months, the 1-year PFS rates were 98% for patients with undetectable MRD who ceased therapy, 96% for patients with undetectable MRD who received continued ibrutinib, and 97% for MRD-positive patients who received continued ibrutinib. All patients did well at 12 months. Knowledge of MRD status to guide discontinuation of therapy did not affect the outcome.[<a href="#cit/section_7.5">

34325</a>

3433] Before MRD is used outside the context of a clinical trial, conclusive evidence is required to establish that MRD is a predictive biomarker that can guide clinical decisions.</p>

3464 <section id="_416">

3466 <h2>

3467Key References for CLL Treatment</h2>

3468

3469 <div id="_section_416" class="pdq-sections">

3470<p id="_417" tabindex="-1">

3471These references have been identified by members of the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment">

3472PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board</a>

3473 as significant in the field of chronic lymphocytic leukemia (CLL) treatment. This list is provided to inform users of important studies that have helped shape the current understanding of and treatment options for CLL. Listed after each reference are the sections within this summary where the reference is cited.</p>

3582 <section id="_129">

3583

3584 <h2>

3585Changes to This Summary (06/30/2023)</h2>

3586

3587 <div id="_section_129" class="pdq-sections">

3588<p id="_130" tabindex="-1">

3589The PDQ cancer information summaries are reviewed regularly and updated as new information becomes available. This section describes the latest changes made to this summary as of the date above.</p>

3590<p id="_1077" tabindex="-1">

3591Editorial changes were made to this summary.</p>

3592<p id="_disclaimerHP_3" tabindex="-1">

3593This summary is written and maintained by the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment">

3594PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board</a>

3595, which is

3596editorially independent of NCI. The summary reflects an independent review of

3597the literature and does not represent a policy statement of NCI or NIH. More

3598information about summary policies and the role of the PDQ Editorial Boards in

3599maintaining the PDQ summaries can be found on the <a href="/types/leukemia/hp/cll-treatment-pdq#_AboutThis_1">

3600About This PDQ Summary</a>

3601 and <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq">

3602PDQ&#174; Cancer Information for Health Professionals</a>

3603 pages.

3604</p>

3605</div>

3610

3611 <section id="_AboutThis_1">

3612

3613 <h2>

3614About This PDQ Summary</h2>

3615

3616 <div id="_section_AboutThis_1" class="pdq-sections">

3617<section id="_AboutThis_2">

3618<h3 id="_AboutThis_2_toc">

3619Purpose of This Summary</h3>

3620<p id="_AboutThis_3" tabindex="-1">

3621This PDQ cancer information summary for health professionals provides comprehensive, peer-reviewed, evidence-based information about the treatment of chronic lymphocytic leukemia. It is intended as a resource to inform and assist clinicians in the care of their patients. It does not provide formal guidelines or recommendations for making health care decisions.</p>

3622</section>

3623<section id="_AboutThis_4">

3624<h3 id="_AboutThis_4_toc">

3625Reviewers and Updates</h3>

3626<p id="_AboutThis_5" tabindex="-1">

3627This summary is reviewed regularly and updated as necessary by the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment">

3628PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board</a>

3629, which is editorially independent of the National Cancer Institute (NCI). The summary reflects an independent review of the literature and does not represent a policy statement of NCI or the National Institutes of Health (NIH).</p>

3630<p id="_AboutThis_22" tabindex="-1">

3631 Board members review recently published articles each month to determine whether an article should:</p>

3632<div class="pdq-content-list">

3633<ul id="_AboutThis_6">

3634<li>

3635be discussed at a meeting,</li>

3636<li>

3637be cited with text, or</li>

3638<li>

3639replace or update an existing article that is already cited.</li>

3640</ul>

3641</div>

3642<p id="_AboutThis_7" tabindex="-1">

3643Changes to the summaries are made through a consensus process in which Board members evaluate the strength of the evidence in the published articles and determine how the article should be included in the summary.</p>

3644<p id="" tabindex="-1">

3645The lead reviewer for Chronic Lymphocytic Leukemia Treatment is:</p>

3646<div class="pdq-content-list">

3647<ul id="">

3648<li>

3649Eric J. Seifter, MD (Johns Hopkins University)</li>

3650</ul>

3651</div>

3652<p id="_AboutThis_9" tabindex="-1">

3653Any comments or questions about the summary content should be submitted to Cancer.gov through the NCI website's <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us" title="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us">

3654Email Us</a>

3655. Do not contact the individual Board Members with questions or comments about the summaries. Board members will not respond to individual inquiries.</p>

3656</section>

3657<section id="_AboutThis_10">

3658<h3 id="_AboutThis_10_toc">

3659Levels of Evidence</h3>

3660<p id="_AboutThis_11" tabindex="-1">

3661Some of the reference citations in this summary are accompanied by a level-of-evidence designation. These designations are intended to help readers assess the strength of the evidence supporting the use of specific interventions or approaches. The PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board uses a <a href="/publications/pdq/levels-evidence/treatment">

3662formal evidence ranking system</a>

3663 in developing its level-of-evidence designations.</p>

3664</section>

3665<section id="_AboutThis_12">

3666<h3 id="_AboutThis_12_toc">

3667Permission to Use This Summary</h3>

3668<p id="_AboutThis_13" tabindex="-1">

3669PDQ is a registered trademark. Although the content of PDQ documents can be used freely as text, it cannot be identified as an NCI PDQ cancer information summary unless it is presented in its entirety and is regularly updated. However, an author would be permitted to write a sentence such as &#8220;NCI&#8217;s PDQ cancer information summary about breast cancer prevention states the risks succinctly: [include excerpt from the summary].&#8221;</p>

3670<p id="_AboutThis_14" tabindex="-1">

3671The preferred citation for this PDQ summary is:</p>

3672<p id="_AboutThis_15" tabindex="-1">

3673PDQ&#174; Adult Treatment Editorial Board. PDQ Chronic Lymphocytic Leukemia Treatment. Bethesda, MD: National Cancer Institute. Updated &lt;MM/DD/YYYY&gt;. Available at: <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/types/leukemia/hp/cll-treatment-pdq" title="https://www.cancer.gov/types/leukemia/hp/cll-treatment-pdq">

3674https://www.cancer.gov/types/leukemia/hp/cll-treatment-pdq</a>

3675. Accessed &lt;MM/DD/YYYY&gt;. [PMID: 26389470]</p>

3676<p id="_AboutThis_16" tabindex="-1">

3677Images in this summary are used with permission of the author(s), artist, and/or publisher for use within the PDQ summaries only. Permission to use images outside the context of PDQ information must be obtained from the owner(s) and cannot be granted by the National Cancer Institute. Information about using the illustrations in this summary, along with many other cancer-related images, is available in <a href="https://visualsonline.cancer.gov/" title="https://visualsonline.cancer.gov/">

3678Visuals Online</a>

3679, a collection of over 2,000 scientific images.

3680

3681</p>

3682</section>

3683<section id="_AboutThis_17">

3684<h3 id="_AboutThis_17_toc">

3685Disclaimer</h3>

3686<p id="_AboutThis_18" tabindex="-1">

3687Based on the strength of the available evidence, treatment options may be described as either &#8220;standard&#8221; or &#8220;under clinical evaluation.&#8221; These classifications should not be used as a basis for insurance reimbursement determinations. More information on insurance coverage is available on Cancer.gov on the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/managing-care" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/managing-care">

3688Managing Cancer Care</a>

3689 page.</p>

3690</section>
